RATING: 9
Wow. I'm surprised it took me this long to get this game. I wasn't keen on racing games before, but this is much more than a racing game. Sure, you're trying to get to the finish line, but that focus has never won me a game yet. Instead, it matters to be the best pirate. you may not come in across the line first, but who cares when you've got all that booty to spend! Seriously, this game has it all. Easy to learn rules, family friendly, a 2 player variant that ADDS TO the game instead of subtracting from it, great components, an AMAZING insert for storage, and a PIRATE THEME! Wow. Again, Wow.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Jamaica is a take on the matter how to make roll-and-move mechanics appeal to more serious gamers. This is achieved by giving the players a degree of control over the movement and adding a layer of resource management to the mix. You can also try to pull of different strategies depending on how much you are into exploring and raiding instead of rushing it to the finish line. The game sure has quite a high luck factor to it but the play time is just right for it not to become an issue. 

Personally I did not fancy Jamaica too much but I would not mind playing it occasionally. Too often I felt that I was not given enough options or the best choice was too obvious. But this is just me wanting to have a meaning to everything.

RATING: 6
A fun pirate racing game.  The cargo hold rule (can't swap out same type of cargo) provides an interesting consideration.  The captain choosing the order of the dice (day/night) provides a nice element of control (when you're the captain).  The card mechanism provides choices while still constraining options.  The treasure cards are a nice addition and incentive, though I think some of them may be a bit overpowered (particularly the saber – I won all my battles, though I lost the game by a hefty margin).  Also, the art is incredible!  Production value is rather nice.

Of course, the big negative is that it's all random.  The battles, the dice, the card draw.  Don't take this one seriously or try to plan too much, it ebbs and flows a lot.  Plus, there's a huge bonus (5 pts) for crossing the finish line.  I think that bonus, and the others on the final 8-10 spaces, may be a bit much.  Seemed to somewhat lessen the need for lots of gold cargo.

A fun game but very random and with a few aspects that may be considered slightly imbalanced.  (Only slightly, not a huge problem.)  The art and production value do give this a nice bump, though.  The reason I rate it a 6 instead of a 7 is because, while it was fun, it wasn't as much fun as other random and/or racing games I've played.  The random elements often feel chaotic and the player often has to choose from the lesser of his undesirable choices.  Yes, part of the game, but annoying at times, nonetheless.

Play this one, it's definitely worth a try, but know that it's pretty random.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Jamaica is a very good game. It can be played by a wide number of players, it's easy to teach, it's quite funny and quick enough to make the people at your table willing to play it a few times in a row. There's a good amount of interaction, that makes everything more spicy.

For these reasons and for the amazing quality of the components and artworks I think that Jamaica is a great gateway game. When I moved to Klagenfurt for my Erasmus scholarship, I faced the situation of introducing people to boargaming and this one worked better than many other games I tried to use (like Ticket to Ride for example).

It is light and easy to teach and pick up quickly; the board, cards and chits etc., all have fantastic artwork; it's possible for somebody way out in front to start with fall back and likewise somebody way at the back initially can catch up and even win the game; I really like that it plays up to 6 comfortably as well. 

This is highly recommended and I am really happy I have a copy of this game in my collection!

RATING: 7
Great theme and fun if you enjoy chaos. 

Complexity - simple, you roll dice and move or get items based on the card you play from your hand. 

Strategy - low, you have limited choices based off randomly drawn cards. 

Luck - high, between dice rolling, random card drawing and treasures that can make or break your chance at winning it can be hard to win consistently. 

Interaction - moderately low, you may want to do a battle to plunder another ships goods or treasure but if things are going your way you will want to stay away from others and if you are far in the lead with a good draw there is nothing others can do to stop you. 

Fun - the theme and battles can add great fun with the outcome making or breaking your chances to win. Anybody can win, even first time players. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9.5
We don't play racing games too often. But the Dice Tower guys talk about this game soooooooo much that we just had to give it a try. And we were not disappointed. Jamaica is a solid game with some of the simplest mechanics put into a game together with some of the best components. You race around the island of Jamaica collecting gold, food and powder in order to outrace and out fight your opponents. Dead simple but so much fun it's almost criminal. Even the two player variant with the Ghost Ship is easy to play unlike most two player variants that involve dummy players. If only that hadn't made the rule book like a treasure map! It makes it such a pain to look up any rules. Fortunately they're aren't a lot of them. Check it out! It won't disappoint!

RATING: 10
[ESP] Un gran juego de carreras, tal vez el que más me ha gustado hasta el momento. PAra todo tipo de jugadores.

En 1675, luego de una larga carrera en piratería, Henry Morgan es designado gobernador de Jamaica, con la explícita orden de limpiar el Caribe de los piratas y bucaneros. En lugar de eso, él invita a sus antiguos colegas y camaradas en armas a unirse a él en su retiro, y así disfrutar de los frutos de sus saqueos en la impunidad.
Cada año, en recuerdo de los "buenos viejos tiempos", Morgan organiza el gran desafío, una carrera alrededor de la isla, en cuyo final el capitán con la mayoría de oro es declarado Gran Ganador.

*********************

Super Ausstattung die zum Spielen einlädt und das erfolgreich auch die Spielemuffel.
Evt. sind Wenigspieler am Anfang etwas unsicher wegen den beiden Phasen (morgens und abends) und befürchten das das Spiel recht komplexer ist. Aber spätestens nach dem 2ten Durchgang sollte eigentlich jeder verstanden haben worauf es ankommt und das man sich dann ganz dem Rennen um die Insel widmen kann. Und das macht schon sehr viel Spass. Der Mix aus Wüfel und Kartenglück sowie das Taktieren mit den beiden Tagesphasen sowie das Haushalten der Resourcen ist auch für Gelegenheitsspieler schnell überschaubar und spannend. Die direkt Nachfrage das Spiel direkt nochmal zu spielen ist auch ein Grund für die gute Beurteilung.

RATING: 8
Initial Impression: The components in this game are gorgeous. Bright colors mixed with cartoony images cover the thick cardboard components. Cute plastic ships that beg to be painted sit in a wonderfully produced insert. The game itself is inviting and accessible for most ages. Surprisingly, the level of depth in the game adjusts to the level of gamer. With children the game can be a simple race. However experienced gamers can introduce a bluffing metagame and take advantage of multiple paths to victory. Do you try to cross the finish line? Do you simply hoard gold? Do you move to attack opponents, hoping that you win the engagement? The choices may seem few, but are interesting.

RATING: 6
Gorgeous artwork and possibly the best box-layout ever seen. Every part has a dedicated place in the box and will stay there even if you toss the box around (but who would do THAT?).

The game is so-so with lower player counts and really starts to get going with 5.
The current turn's captain – the player who rolls and determines the dice order – should pay attention to not overthink the dice order (and double check with his available action cards). This would result in dead time for the other players who are just waiting to see the dice order, so that they can figure out what they want to do this turn.

RATING: 6
A fun little game, that would be great for families.  It is a simple design and plays in a nice short timeframe.  Balancing out when to advance your ship in the race and when to stock up makes for some great decisions.  There is a lot of luck, especially in the combat, but it's a fairly light game so I don't mind the luck.

What sets this game apart is the art and components.  This game is absolutely gorgeous, and that just adds to the theme.  I'm not usually a huge fan of race games or pirate-themed games, but this one just seems to work so well.  Some players will argue that there is way too much randomness, and therefore it's not for gamers.  However this is easily remedied by increasing the players' handsize.  When a player has more cards to choose from there will be less luck and more strategy.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Ray

RATING: 9
This beautifully illustrated game is a fairly simple one about pirates racing around the island of jamaica and trying to collect treasure and points along the way. The main hook in this game is that your ship has a certain number of spots for either gold, food or gun powder, and when you get more of anything, it MUST go in an empty spot, or replace things in a spot. You cannot combine loot that you get even if it's the same type, which leads to interesting choices.

Very fun and simple enough to be gateway, give it a try if the theme is even vaguely appealing.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Lightweight nautical race game with large doses of luck, based on both the cards in your hand and the dice rolls before each round. Saying that, I played this with a bunch of serious, grown up, gamers and I haven't laughed so much at any boardgame. 

The game rules are simple, it's a fun concept and there's enough planning and combat in there to keep things interesting. We laughed most when people got their move cards mixed up and ended up sailing backwards. We wondered if it would be possible to sail round the whole board backwards, but decided you couldn't do it! Looting each others holds was also fun, as was me repeatedly correctly calling my own misfortune in combat.

Jamaica should become a "fun for all the family" classic, given time.

RATING: 7
Almost a pure light game, but rated light medium due to the difficulty encountered at times when selecting a card for your 2 actions. Sometimes a player must discern between the lesser of two evils, i.e., do I move into combat or sit and take resources while falling further behind? Combat is a little random, and can make a difference in progress around the board unless card play is carefully selected. Fortunately, losers usually don't get hurt too much. Otherwise, we enjoy this race/collection resource game with a few decisions, but offering a decent amount of fun. With 4 it is more of a race game; 5 and 6 players encounter more conflict and adds a level of difficulty avoiding other players. A hit at every level of gamer experience, save perhaps the diehard strategist. The sheer fun of sailing around the island with others competing for the few treasures in a race for home base is earns this game a high rating despite occasional frustrating dice results for actions.
Includes the 4 cards in the Extra Treasures expansion.

RATING: 6
I too had high expectations after watching some video reviews here on the geek. However, I don’t think the game is that good, even considering it’s a light family game. It’s actually not so light as I had thought, at least during your first play. I’ve tried it with 3 and 6, and both numbers worked well, although I imagine the sweet spot would be 4 or 5. With 3, there isn’t as much tension and the battles are far between. With 6, the downtime is noticeable and bogs down an otherwise light game.

There is definitely room for clever gameplay, but at the end of the day, you’re rolling a lot of dice (although the two dice are used by everybody in the same round, which I like) and drawing cards randomly, so it’s hard to plan too much ahead, especially as you only have 3 cards available each round. Still, I’ve experienced some extremely clever play when players move forward and cannot pay the cost, and thereby moving back towards a pirate cove and gaining a treasure! These treasures can be worth a significant amount of points (I actually won one of my games when I had the two 7 point treasure tile although I also had the -3 point’er – but that did kind of rubbed me the wrong way as the runner-up was the one who ended in Port Royal with me far behind, and he even had a -4 point curse)… I think that the treasure deck is a brilliant idea, and all of the treasures are useful in their own ways, although some are definitely better than others.

I like that you need to pay food or coins in order to advancing around the island and be the first one to cross the line. Although you don’t necessarily win by crossing the line first, you do have an advantage, but if you’ve stacked up on a lot of gold you might win as well. Just be aware that the other players can attack you if they land in the same spot as you, and this can be quite a luckfest due to the die-roll. The production value is obviously astonishing and helps drawing your family in. It’s a nice light game that probably overstays its welcome with 6, but maybe that was in part due to the fact that we didn’t roll a single 6, so we moved forwards slowly. Definitely not a bad game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
[b]Includes Jamaica: The Extra Treasures[/b]

Jamaica is, for me, a hidden gem of a family game. It's a racing game, and pretty much anyone can get behind the concept of a racing game. It has some dice and hand management of cards, which players use to move forward or backward, or gather up food, or gold, or guns. It has dice chucking combat, and spots where you pick up treasure. It's simply a nice combination of relatively simple rules and fun gameplay. Oh... and it plays up to six.

The game is also gorgeously produced, with artwork on the cards that show pictorial story if you lay them from left to right. Sure it's random, and sure it's light, but given it's weight and length, I'm hard-pressed to think of a better family game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
A fun racing game that is good gateway and family game material. Great production across the board for sure and was likely top of its class 9 years ago when it came out. However, it feels just a little fiddly with the moving of goods back and forth from your holds. Yet the battles you have are quick and almost entirely based on the luck of a die roll. It seems like these two ideas contradict each other.

The thing holding this game back for me is that I have played Colt Express and enjoy that game much more. It just removes that small piece of moving all the goods around and in my mind focuses so much more interaction than Jamaica and makes it a more suitable family game with more laughs and more enjoyment.

RATING: 5
This was pretty painful to play. The components are nice, but it really felt like the game was playing me. The decisions you have to make are not as important as I'd like them to be. Because your holds are so limited, most of what you take early will be turned over a couple times before you get to the end. 

I wish there were more ways to be able to 'bank' some of your gold prior to the end.  There is no way to really defend it from other pirates, since you're constantly bumping into people hand fighting battles (which you initiate even if you're woefully outgunned). 

The one caveat I have here is that this is a great game for a family with young children. They can easily grasp the theme and the rules, and there is enough chaos/luck (boy is there!) that the young ones can compete pretty evenly with mom and dad. It wouldn't be my first choice for a game for that purpose, but you could do a lot worse.

RATING: 6
Roll and move racing game.  It's made more interesting by some user control over movement and direction (forward or back).  The start player rolls two dice then decides how to place them: one must be a day action and one must be a night action.  All players have an identical deck of action cards.  Each card has two actions, a day side and a night side.  The actions are taken according to the number of the die placed in that position.  All players decide, from the drawn cards in hand, which to play.  I'd play again but am not likely to purchase this.

RATING: 9
Update: many years later, this has proven itself time and again as the king of games for non-serious gamers. The fact that it scales to 6 with very little downtime bumps it from 8 to 9.

I hate to say it, but I actually agree with Tom Vasel. Awesome game. DSP? No? SdJ? Sure. Just pure family fun. By far the most beautiful components to a game I've seen in a long long time. And by components I mean the cards. The board is fine, but the cards are over the top. I'm happy just looking at them without even playing. This is a pirate racing game. Sounds silly, right? It is. And that's why it works. Of course what kind of pirate racing game would be complete without needing food for your crew, finding treasure, getting cannons to blast other people's ships, and stealing their booty? Check. Check. Check. I actually find the game to be fairly clever, even beyond the great art and silliness. There's an interesting mechanic where each player gets a hand of three cards, where each cards has two actions, morning and night. But the magnitude of the actions (e.g. how far to move forward or backward, how much gold, food or cannons to collect) is determined by dice. One person rolls, then chooses which to assign to morning and which to evening. After seeing, everyone chooses one of their cards simultaneously, and then turns are resolved.

RATING: 6.5
What I like about this race game is the speed of play, the quality of the components, the depth of the artwork and that every choice is really 2 choices in one.

What bothers me a bit is the randomness - there's so much that it can put one unlucky player very far behind.  I think this could potentially be fixed by letting players have more than 3 cards to choose from each round.  Maybe you get your whole deck to start and then run through them until you're out?

That being said - some strong potential here.

RATING: 6
Components: Beautiful board, nice tokens and dice, and absolutely gorgeous cards (forming an incredible panoramic view from the perspective of a drinking pirate); the best cards I've seen. The insert is also well designed. I like the treasure map aspect of the rules.

Experience: Fun. There are simple yet interesting decisions to be made on each turn, just trying to balance my load, manage my cards, and hoard treasure. There is enough variety to the course (with the three forks, the skull coves, and the variously-numbered ports and open sea spaces) to keep it fresh. Very tactical.

RATING: 6
A pirate racing game.  Collect food, gold, gunpowder, and treasure.  Pay food/gold to land on certain spaces.  Land on the same square as an opponent and do combat.  Spend gunpowder for advantage; winner gets some loot from loser.  

Interesting action mechanisms with the cards.  Actions allowed include moving forward or backward, and collecting resources (gold, food, gunpowder).  Dice roll determines the quantity of goods or number of movement.  

This game serves as a go-to game with non-gamers.  It's got great-looking bits and board, is easy to grasp, and is over before it becomes too boring for me.

RATING: 8.7
A fun racing game with a pirate them and simple rules. Each player has a pirate ship and five holds in which you can store gold, food or gunpowder. The "captain" roles two dice, places them on day and night spaces, each player picks an action card, then you do what the card says. You need food to travel through most sea spaces, gold for ports, and gunpowder for battles. In addition, there are nine pirate lairs with a variety of treasures that cost nothing to move into. The first to circumnavigate the island gets 15 bonus gold; the most gold wins. Has great aesthetics, up there with Tikal, Zombicide, and Descent. A bit more luck-centered than most games on this list.

RATING: 6
Old school race game where players race their pirate ship around the island of Jamaica.  One player rolls a pair of dice, and players select their cards to define their "morning" and "evening" actions for the turn.  Actions are movement, or loading (food, gold or gunpowder).  Game ends when one player completes a lap, and players are awarded points for progress, gold obtained, and treasure.  Fun game, feels a bit like Hase und Igel.  Enjoyed it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
I love the gorgeous board, artwork, and components, and the box insert is expertly designed.  The theme is really fun to play with casual gamers. I'm also a big fan of the simulaneous action planning mechanic. The game is very easy to teach, although the layout of the rulebook is a bit awkward.  My only complaint is the amount of luck involved in winning the game. I don't mind luck in a game, especially one this thematic, but the luck to skill ratio seems a bit high in this one, especially with the large variance of the attack die.  Luckily, this is the kind of game that is still really fun regardless of what place you're in, so I still enjoy it a lot.

RATING: 10
This is one of the most unique games I have ever played. The card play in this game adds a very strategic dimension to a fairly generic racing game. There are two actions on each card. Not to mention, that you get to blow your friends out of the water and steal their gold :)!!

RATING: 7.25
A light filler game with a fair bit of randomness that’s best played with people that are not so serious. 
   
However I am not a fan of the artwork: I feel there is strong disconnect between the gameplay and the Disney-inspired art.  The artwork makes the game look like its aimed at children under 12 and puts it in the same realm as Candy Land.  However, while the mechanics of the game are simple, they aren’t as simple (or even appropriate) as Candy Land which is what the game looks like.  

While the cut-throat tactic of battling other players (which is often out of your control) and the discontent of working hard to obtain treasure only to find out its cursed, may correlate well with the Pirate theme, it may likely cause too much grief and doesn’t exactly instill the best of values (or behavior) for the very same young children that the art aims the game towards.  Unless of course you are trying to encourage you children to attack other children and steal their plunder.  Imagine Candy Land where players obtain candy along the way, but when another player comes along and lands on the same spot, they get to steal the other child’s candy.  Older children can handle this, but then older children might be put off with the childish artwork here.  

The child-geared artwork also tends to put off a lot of adults; you are essentially playing a game that looks like Candy Land.  I would very much like to see the artwork in this game redone with a slightly more mature look and see how people take to the game.  It would be a great experiment to see if adults take to game more if it was re-themed with cover art from the show “Black Sails” for example.  And give us some plastic and better looking doubloons!, not the corny looking cardboard ones with cartoon skulls on them – the ones sold in party stores look better than these.  

However, my rating here is based on the actual gameplay, not the artwork.

RATING: 8
This is a pirate-themed tactical race game with player interaction and side goals (e.g. detouring for treasure). The winner is the player who best balances their position in the race with their success at the side goals.

Setting: Jamaica, 1675.
After a long career in piracy, Captain Henry Morgan skillfully gets appointed to be Governor of Jamaica, with the explicit order to cleanse the Caribbean of pirates and buccaneers! Instead, he invites all of his former "colleagues" to join him in his retirement, to enjoy the fruits of their looting with impunity. Each year, in remembrance of the "good old days," Morgan organizes the Great Challenge, a race around the island, and at its end, the Captain with the most gold is declared Grand Winner.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Even though Jamaica is technically a pirate-themed racing game, it feels like a lighter version of Pirate's Cove. But even though it's fairly lightweight, there's a lot of fun to be had here. Movement is done through a fairly ingenious joint dice/card system, and there's a little bit of strategy to be had when figuring out whether to fill up your hold with coins, food or gunpowder or make a beeline for the finish. Combat is a bit too luck-driven for me; even if you have loads of gunpowder and treasure cards to add to your dice roll, you can be wiped out by that nasty "instant kill" face on the combat die. But those minor misgivings are allayed by the sheer fun of this game.

Jamaica deserves special mention for its production quality. This has to be the best presentation of a board game I've ever seen. The artwork is bright and cartoony without being cheesy, the board is gorgeous, and there's not a sub-par component to be found. Jamaica also has the most functional box insert imaginable; every single component has a clearly-defined home, and nothing loses its place even if the box is placed on its side or turned upside down. This game really is a work of art.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Really interesting race game but still very simple. Components are really nice quality and the box insert is very nice. The artwork is exceptional with the card art lining up to give one long image cut into the seven cards.

Cards have two actions morning and evening, two dice are rolled and placed on either morning or evening. The number of pips indicates how many times you may repeat the action, then you pay gold/food/ collect treasure or fight dependent upon the space you stopped in. Then evening occurs in the same way as morning.

There are bonus points for finishing first however these seemed a little high after only one game as the winner had 25 points to second places 7, 15 of which came from the first place.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I've played this twice and both games left me dissatisfied. The first game I just struggled to make my boat move at all. The second game I struggled to make my boat move, and when I finally got going, I had little chance of winning. The game looks great, it's all visual which I like, it's got nice mechanisms. It just does not work as a race. The choice of actions of the cards is 6to5 against forward moves. I'd like to see a bigger card deck with more choices. It's a nice game for what it is, but what it is is not a race.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.2
This is a stupid little pick up & race game, that for who knows what reason I enjoyed.  It is too simple for my gaming groups, and probably too repetitive, and too dicey.  I shouldn't like it, but I do.  I will keep this on hand for children, and adults wanting some simple games.  I want to play it with them.

I admit I was predisposed to liking it because I was attracted to the colors & graphics pictured and as I unpacked it I was very pleased to see great looking components that fit very nicely into a well designed insert (no need to bag here).  The simple rules are laid out in a colorful poster format. Took 10 mins to read, and only a few minutes to set up.  

It is a simple race where pirates pick up loot, have to pay out some gold & food now & then, and battle a little too, and then return to port--the one with the most gold wins.  The box says 45 mins, but can be played faster than that with 3 people.  I like it with more people (5 is best, 6 makes it a little too long for what it is) because there is more combat for what is in a ship's hold (Battle is short & easy). Pirates in the lead tend to collect all the treasures, so if those in the rear must catch them to wrestle the treasures away.  Combat fits well into the theme because this is a raucous group of Henry Morgan's undisciplined pirates who race their ships, and being criminals, they do anything the drunken sots like to win the race.

RATING: 8
"Jamaïca", c'est un simple jeu de parcours, ni plus, ni moins. Oui, mais un jeu de parcours intelligent, où ce n'est pas forcément le premier arrivé qui gagne. Non, car il y a plein de petits paramètres qui viennent enrichir l'ensemble. Tout d'abord, il y a le choix de l'ordre des dés, qui est un mécanisme très réussi et qui va déterminer l'ordre des actions. Premier choix pour celui qui lance les dés en fonction de ses cartes (qu'est ce qui m'arrange le plus ?), puis choix pour les autres joueurs qui, en fonction de cet ordre, déterminent eux-aussi l'action qui leur semble la meilleure. Mais dans une main limitée à trois cartes seulement, il faut donc choisir de laquelle on se débarrasse et lesquelles on garde pour un jet qui leur conviendrait peut-être mieux.

Au-delà de cette mécanique assez intéressante et qui permet une petite maîtrise du hasard, le jeu regorge de petits détails qui rendent l'ensemble très plaisant à jouer : le parcours qui se sépare, le coût des cases d'arrivée, les trésors à récolter au fur et à mesure, l'organisation des cales de chaque navire... Bref, malgré des règles simplissimes, très vite expliquées, très bien rédigées (il faut noter le travail exécuté sur celles-ci, c'est très intuitif et on trouve très vite la réponse à une question), le jeu a tout juste assez de subtilités pour en faire un jeu certes d'abord familial, mais non dénué d'intérêts et avec une réelle richesse.

Le petit point noir, c'est peut-être le système de combat. Prendre de la poudre permet un certain avantage, mais la stratégie peut être ruinée et nos doublons (qui rapportent quand même beaucoup lors du décompte final) être dérobés sur un simple jet de dé chanceux de l'adversaire qui vous envoie six pieds sous mer, alors même que cet adversaire n'avait aucun avantage au combat. Un joueur qui n'aurait donc plus rien à perdre pourrait combattre sans cesse, jouant uniquement sur sa chance aux dés (ou sur la malchance de ses adversaires), ce qui rend la partie assez désagréable. Un système comme celui de "Deadwood", où le combat se joue aussi aux dés, me semble plus juste, bien que la chance puisse aussi jouer, elle me semble plus maîtrisée que dans "Jamaïca". Les mauvais jets de dés pour les actions, eux, sont moins graves, tout le monde subissant les mêmes tirages.

Mis à part ce bémol, "Jamaïca" est un jeu qui, selon moi, aurait pu/du rencontrer plus de succès auprès du grand public, tant il convient à une audience familiale, tant ses règles sont simples et claires, tant le jeu apporte un vrai plaisir ludique rapide et efficace, sans être brise-neurones. Pour les gros joueurs, le plaisir est sans doute moindre, mais je considère que c'est par ce type de jeux que le public peut s'ouvrir et découvrir de nouvelles choses, parfois plus complexes. Et puis, même si on est gros joueur, quelque chose de plus light de temps à autre, ça ne fait pas de mal. Et matière de jeu light, "Jamaïca" est sans doute ce qui se fait de mieux, ou presque. Alors oui, c'est un simple jeu de parcours et certains diront que le thème est plaqué. On pourrait bien sûr le remplacer par un autre, mais personnellement, je trouve qu'il est en parfaite adéquation avec le sentiment de jeu et les mécanismes mis en place. Même le coup d'une action le matin et une l'après-midi, assez artificiel, arrive à donner un petit plus thématique à l'ensemble.

Ajoutez à cela un matériel irréprochable, et vous obtenez un des jeux que je choisirais sans doute si je devais faire découvrir le jeu de société moderne à des non initiés.

RATING: 6
A gorgeously designed race game with a Pirate theme and some light, fun mechanics not totally devoid of decision making.  There is a lot of randomness in this one, but the player that can best manage the onslaught of these elements will be the victor.  Jamaica is in no means a game of great substance, and is one I would, and have, openly deterred "Gamers" away from.  However, even though this may not be an outing for the more seasoned, and disgruntled among us Jamaica can offer a splendid and fun romp with a strong weight/time ratio.  Plus it allows for a solid gateway type game to host a pirate theme.  Gorgeous, not spectacular, but can be loads of fun.

RATING: 6
After 1st Play: it's still a bit beyond my 4.5 year old son, so he and his mom teamed up to control the Red Ship.  This was our first play and we've got a few rules questions to look up, but it's nice, quick, light, beautiful, accessible, and interesting.  Glad I traded for this.

I'll keep looking, but in the meantime, this is pretty enough to capture and maintain his interest, and short enough that it doesn't take longer than it needs to.

RATING: 6.7
Beautiful game visually. Even the box looks good, like a treasure chest. The game itself is fun, but can be confusing to decide which way to play your cards for some people. There's not too much depth, but there are some tactically fun things to do, like stealing other pirate's gold, food stores and treasures(cards), or giving curses(cards) and blowing each other out of the water. It is also a race, with the winner being the one to balance their finish position with their quantity of gold, plus the treasure and curse cards which give plus or minus points. With four of us, it plays in about 45 minutes.

RATING: 7
2008 acquisition.  Rating is currently for 2-player games only.

This is a one of the most beautifully made game I own.  From the map to the beautifully illustrated cards, to the way everything fit perfectly together in the box, all make a good impression even before you play the game.

It is also, in my book, a very wife/SO/GF/etc-friendly game.  It has dice (always an important component to the wife) but a manageable randomness the way you can change the order of the dice rolled.  It plays in a relatively short time, and you can choose to be as confrontational or not as you like.

RATING: 7
A fun, hectic racing game with a cool pirate theme. Part strategy and part luck, this game is more about the enjoyment during the race rather then finishing first. Personally I really like the simultaneous action selection element; it really speeds up the game and adds some fun chaos.

There's a take-that element with combat that involves a potential instant-win die-roll. That's usually the one part of the game that gets the most complaints.

Other then that the game has an insert, which is great! The rule book is shaped like a treasure map, which is bad. It sounds fun but is unwieldy in practice. Overall a fun game that's a bit too light to see a lot of play, but still worth keeping and bringing out every once in a while.

RATING: 8
Really fun and with an excellent presentation! A pirate race around Jamaica, where players collect treasure, feed their crew and fight their opponents along the way. One of the few racing games where going back is a valid and viable choice (sometimes).

It has a lot of really good ideas, the main three being the dice allocation, the limited storage and the ending.

Every round the main player rolls two D6 and assigns one to the "day" and another to the "night". Each player is holding three cards, each with a "day" and a "night" action. The players pick a card for the round, and each action will be multiplied by the number on the die,

The ships have a 5 slots for storage. Each time you get something you have to fit it in one of them, but if there's no room you have to throw something out.

When a player has made it all the way around the island, the player with the most loot wins! It's not necessarily the one in first place.

Fun!

RATING: 6
:star::star::star::nostar::nostar:
There's a lot of neat stuff here, so I'm tempted to bump it up to four stars.

Players are pirates racing around the island of Jamaica. A combination of die rolls and simultaneous card play determines how far you move or how many of the various goods you pick up. Each space has a cost of either food or gold that can send you backwards if you're not prepared. Battles for spaces occur frequently and add some take-that excitement. There's a nice bonus for winning the race (or placing well), but it's no guarantee for winning the game with most gold.

The artwork is cartoony, detailed, and beautiful. The production overall is very nice. It offers a lot of fun and good player interaction. The randomness of the dice and card draws should keep it fresh after repeated plays, even though the play itself may become repetitive.

Definitely a good pick for competitive families.

RATING: 6.5
A nice little race game, with a fair bit of chaos. One player rolls 2 dice indicating a quantity for day and night, then everyone simultaneously chooses 1 card from 3 in their hand which depicts two actions.. these will either be moving forward/backward, or loading goods (food,gold,ammo).. ships that move onto the same space must fight by spending ammo and each rolling a die. The game ends when the first player reaches the finish line, and points are awarded for how far you got, and also how much gold you collected.

Components are very nice, but the gameplay is very light and rather random.

Played 5 times so far, with anywhere from 3 to 6 players.

RATING: 7.5
Wonderfully themed with beautiful graphics and some clever ideas, but after playing it online a few times, it seems as though there's little to no actual strategy or tactics involved.  You could get stuck with no arrow cards at all for a while, or with one arrow card but snake eyes on the dice...  There are some choices that are meaningful, but mostly it's pretty random. I don't mind (and often enjoy) some randomness in a game, but it is quite heavy here.  Regardless, it's really fun in a mostly mindless way and I've enjoyed playing several games online and was happy to pick it up in a trade.  I have no doubt that this would probably be a good "gateway game", and I think it could benefit from a couple of simple variant tweaks to make it a little bit less random for more of a gamer's game.  I think the ideal number of players is definitely 2-4.  With the full measure of 6 it all gets bunched up and there are a lot of battles where everyone loses the things that they need to travel, so I think it goes on a bit long for that many people.  Otherwise, it's definitely fun and plays more fluidly (and still with some good conflict) with 2-4.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
The game is about pirates racing around an island, but it's not an actual race game, as the winner is the player with most gold in the end. The idea of attributing dice to day and night actions that are then selected with a single card is interesting, but luck still is a huge factor.

The point swing from treasure cards alone would be enough to ruin it for serious players (there are even cards with negative values), but the occasional combats are even worse. If a player ends a movement on the same space as an opponent, they must battle. They simply roll a die, adding any gunpowder they committed, and compare results, with the winner taking a card or the contents of a cargo hold from the loser. And just to make it more random, there is a die face that is an automatic victory, regardless of how much gunpowder the other player spent.

The very nice card art, cartoony and kid-friendly, adds to the broad appeal of the pirate theme. This certainly can be a good game for families with children, and that seems to be its target audience, but there is just too much randomness to recommend it for gamers.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
JEM 20. szám: 
Mindenki egy neves kalózt játszik, aki a hajójával minél eredményesebben próbál célba érni. Mindenki kap egy vitorlást 11 akciókártyát és egy hajórakteret ábrázoló lapkát, aminek rekeszeibe áruk he¬lyezhetők el, kezdésként az egyikbe 3 arany, a másikba 3 élelem. 
A táblát, amin a verseny zajlik, előkészítjük: 9 megadott helyre felhelyezünk 1-1 lefordított kincslapkát, a kincskártyákat pedig, amelyeket akkor kapunk meg, ha a kincslapkákat tartalmazó mezőkre lépünk, egy adott helyre, megkeverve és lefordítva. Ezek között találunk olyat, ami sima győzelmi pontot ad; továbbá olyat, ami átkozott, és ezáltal győzelmi pontot vesz el tőlünk a játék végén; és képességkártyákat, amikkel pl. több árut szállíthatunk, stb. 
	Minden játékos felhúz 3-3 akciókártyát a saját készletéből, majd a kezdőjátékos dob 2 és eldönti, hogy melyik legyen a „reggeli”, azaz első akció száma, illetve melyik legyen az „estié”, a másodiké. Kijátszik egy kártyát, a többit visszateszi a saját paklijára, a kijátszott kártyáról viszont mindkét akciót végrehajtja, majd ugyanígy a többiek is óramutató járá¬sa szerinti sorrendben végre¬hajtják mindkét akciójukat. 2 lehetséges akció van: a moz¬gás (előre vagy hátra) és a rakodás (élelmet, puskaport vagy aranyat). Minden körben a kezdőjátékos a saját kártyáira optimalizálja az akciók számát, amit viszont a többieknek követni kell, tehát nekik is ugyanannyi reggeli és esti akciót kell végrehajtaniuk. 
Külön szabályok vonatkoznak a kétszemélyes játékra, ahol a fekete hajó mindig a szellemhajó szerepét játssza el harmadik játékosként, és mozgására eltérő szabályok vonatkoznak. Ha mozgás során üres mezőre lépünk, akkor kifizetjük az ott feltüntetett árat (aranyat vagy élelmet), illetve ritka esetben ingyenes az odalépés, és még egy kincskártyát is kapunk Érdekesebben alakul, ha az érkezési mező nem üres – ekkor ütközetre kerül sor. Ez a játékos eldönti, hogy beveti-e raktáraiból a puskaport (ezek mindegyike 1 pontot ér), és dob a harci kockával, majd ugyanezt megteszi a támadott játékos is, és akinek végül több pontja van, az nyer. Ez egy rend-kívül egyszerű csatamechanizmus, így látszik, hogy nem is ez a játék gerince – valószínűleg azért került bele, hogy megoldja a már foglalt mezőkre érkező újabb játékosok problémáját. A vesztes hajó marad, ahol volt, a nyertes pedig elveheti a vesztes egy rekeszének teljes tartalmát vagy egy kincskártyáját, de akár egy képességet adó kártyáját is. És hogy egy kicsit a kibabrálás szellemét is behozzuk a játékba: a nyertes rátukmálhatja a másikra egy saját mínuszpontos kártyáját. Berakodás során, ha van üres rekeszünk, akkor betesszük az árut, ha viszont nincs, akkor egy rekeszt kiürítünk (visszatesszük az árut a bankba), azonban a kidobott és az újonnan berakodott áru nem lehet ugyanaz. 
A játék akkor ér véget, amikor valaki elér a Port Royal mezőre, azaz megtett egy teljes kört. Ha ezt a reggeli ak-cióval tette meg, akkor az estit már nem hajtja végre, a többiek viszont még végigcsinálják a maguk körét, hogy mindenkinek azonos számú köre legyen. Az a győztes, aki a legtöbb pontot gyűjtötte, ami 3 részből tevődik össze: A célmezőn és az azt megelőző néhány mezőn győzelmi pontszámok olvashatók, ezeket megkapja az, aki ott tar¬tózkodik a játék végén. A gyűjtött aranyanként 1-1 pont. A gyűjtött kincsek, mínusz az elátkozott kártyák pontjai. Ha valaki a -5-ös mezőn vagy az előtt állva fejezi be a versenyt, akkor pontjaiból 5-öt levonunk 

Összességében egy szép kivitelű családi játék, amelyben az egymással való csata illetve kiszúrás nem kapott túlzott mértéket így gyerekekkel is jól játszható (főleg ha fiúk azok, akik vevők a kalózos témákra).
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
A "roll-and-move" game done right. I love the theme of this game: Racing Pirates! Each player represents a different historical pirate. The goal of the game is to simply have the most points by the end of the race. The end is triggered when the first person crosses Port Royal (which is where the race began). But here's the catch. The first person to cross isn't necessarily the winner. You get points by how well you finished (i.e. 1st, 2nd, ect.) AND by how many gold doubloons and hidden treasures you amassed! These are gained by, well, being pirates! Looting each other and all sorts of swashbuckling are highly encouraged.

The components in this game are top notch. No expense was spared (within reason of course, I mean you're not playing with REAL gold doubloons).

RATING: 8
December 2015 update: bumping my score up after some more plays. I'm seeing more of the joy in this game. It works brilliantly as a gateway, and the art dazzles every time I get it out. I do still dislike the luck-of-the-draw aspect, though: if only one player has the double-forward card in their hand on a big roll, kiss the game goodbye.

This is a pretty fun little game, although I admit I was hoping for more. I bought it because Sam and Zee (of Dice Tower fame) speak so highly of it so often.

The artwork is absolutely tremendous, the component quality is top notch, the "day/night" mechanic is clever, and it's easy to learn and fairly fun to play. It's a good gateway or filler+.

But since everybody has the same deck, draw order basically determines everything. I often feel like I don't really have much in the way of compelling decisions, and it can have a HUGE runaway leader problem where somebody rockets into the lead and stays there.

It just seems to miss a little bit of "oomph" for me. It's not bad at all, just not as good as I hoped.

RATING: 7
First played Feb 26th, 2009. Taught in 10min, played in 45+min with 5 players. Good light game with good luck/strategy mix. Each player is given a ship 3 gold and 4 food to start. Each player has a deck of cards as well(shuffle and start with three). You race around the island of Jamaica with the first back ending the game. Each gold is worth 1pt, there are special VP cards. You also get VPs for how close you finish with 15pts as the max. You can get negative VPs with cards too and even if you don't finish close enought to the finish. There are many spaces around the island. When you land on a space, you are required to pay food (2-4), gold (3-7), pirate space (draw a card), or free space. If you land on a space with another pirate, you attack them with the winner getting one spot of booty (nothing happens in ties). The start player rolls two dice and decide which dice will be the morning and night dice. Your deck of cards has activities on them(movement forward/backwards, get food, get gold, get gun powder) whenever you get a comodity you place it in one of your 5 hull that are empty or toss out what's in there or what you get. Quick easy fun game worth giving a try for those with simple rules.

RATING: 10
Usually when I give a game a 10 rating it is because of the game mechanics and the level of "grit" (challenge/suspense) experienced during play. I don't normally take into consideration artwork, playing pieces or box design. Especially box design. I only take design (eye appeal) and game pieces into consideration before buying a game.  Jamiaca has totally blown me away! Not only in game mechanics but also in the artwork and, AND box design.

The game mechanics, in my opinion, are solid. Even for two players. Play was a tremendous hit with all of us whom have played so far.

The art work is absolutely beautiful. The artist really put a lot of thought into things. For example, the treasure chests on the treasure cards; depending on the point value of the cards the chests look (from varying degrees) barren, to sightly stocked, to overflowing with jewels and gold. 

Lastly, the box. The time that went into the box insert - WOW! There is a place for everything and when the lid is in place you can stand the box up on end or flip it over and everything stays snugly in place. Bravo!

I know of no other game that I own or have played that meets game design/mechanics, artwork and storage consideration. I'm an Axis & Allies die-hard and an very much into similar strategic type games, Jamaica however, as of right now, is my most favorite game.  

I discovered that there were some promo cards that, of course, are no longer available. We'll, that didn't stop me. I made my own. And you can't tell them apart from the original cards available in the game.WOOT! I'll post pictures along with instructions of how I made them in the morning.

RATING: 3
2013-07-15

Initial Rating: 5.0 (April 2010)

I dislike racing games AND I dislike pirate games (thanks to merchants & Marauders), so in the theme department Jamaica lost a lot of points with me. Jamaica was one of the first games I ever played, on 2010 I liked almost every game I played, still I didn’t have fun playing Jamaica so I rated it a 5.0 at the time.

The rulebook seems like a treasure map. It seemed like a neat idea at the beginning, but it makes hard to review it quickly, also if you only look the big points you can miss some of the rules explained in smaller letters at the bottom. The game has too much luck for my liking AND it is way too light for me. 

On the good side, the game is gorgeous, the components are very well done, and Jamaica is perfect to play with your family or non-gamer friends. The rules can be explained under 5 minutes.

I don’t expect to buy it ever although I can (perhaps) play again with a boardgame newbie.

Current Rating: 3.0

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
On a turn the player rolls two dice and decides which will be the morning action and which the evening action. Then players select from their top three cards which one to play. Players can use the actions to move, or get gold, food, or cannons. Some spaces make you pay food or gold. When players land on another players ship they can fight. The fight is based on dice rolls but can be modified by cannons. Try to finish first or be near the first place finisher to gain some victory points, and then have plenty of gold for additional victory points. It's a very fun game.

RATING: 7
Seems like a pretty exemplary family game if there ever was one.  Relatively simple rules, quick playtime, good amount of decision making to keep everyone interested, what more could you ask for?  The theme is pretty thin (and not very relevant), though this is easily glossed over when you see the quality components.  Everyone I've played with has verbally noted the high quality of the artwork and components - they are truly very well done.  I've only played with 4 players, but I'd like to try with 5 or 6, since it seems like a good game for a larger group, both in terms on interaction and lack of significant added downtime.  There's nothing terribly new or original about the design, but it seems like a game that would improve with further play and I look forward to playing this a lot more.

RATING: 8
WORST RULEBOOK EVER. Honestly, of all the hundreds of games I have played, I have not come across the sheer stupidity of a publisher who has made the mistake of a fold-out rulebook like this.

That aside, the game itself is quite fun. It's a very simple light filler, but the components really sell the theme. Players are pirates racing around Jamaica trying to balance between gunpowder, food and gold.

My one gripe (aside from the rulebook idiocy) is that the action deck is pretty small and gets reshuffled too often in a game. And because each player has the same deck, it often ends up that players mimic each others move. Otherwise a solid, not-too-thinky race game to kill some time.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
This is my kind of race game.  The kind where you can be behind, but only because your best turn hasn't come yet.  The kind where on your way back up the ladder, you can win combat and clear out a hull full of gold.  Leads can be deceptive in this game and you must straddle the line between offense and defense carefully.  Planning and resource management is crucial in preparation for what may come your way.  

Components are top notch, the art is wonderful, and the gameplay is very rewarding.  New players tend to struggle on their first play, not understanding that they only have 1 of those "double green arrow" cards to spend. The rule book, while thematic, should not have been a treasure map.  Referencing the rules feels like holding up a giant newspaper.  

You should have this game if you want a more complex race game.

RATING: 7
Replaced Pirates Cove for me as a light Family style Pirate themed game. I think it takes a second play to appreciate more as during the first play you don't realize as much just how fast you could move forward if you wanted to ( save your double green arrow card for that five/six roll).  Even then it's not so simple a decision as there is treasure and wealth gain that need to be balanced a bit against simply springing ahead the fastest.

There is some randomness in the treasure card draw but overall it has a satisfying amount of meaningful decisions for a lighter game (Even the good old 'Do you let the negative backward movement card(s) clutter up your hand or do you play them anyway at an opportune time to help maximize your choices later on?'.

I've also picked up Black Fleet so will have to see if there is room for both in our collection or not.  Certainly for a heavier pirate themed game there is Merchants and Mauraders.

RATING: 5.5
I had high expectations for this game and I won't mention what they were based on. When you here the rules explained- the game sounds like it is ideal. Quick, light and yet somehow strategic. 

Unfortunately all decisions you make have very small impact on your success. First, because of the battle dice roll. You could build your strategy around winning fights by gathering powder. But then it often doesn't matter because the dice can easily negate all your efforts. It's just random. Second- this "luck" thing is totally present in every aspect of the game. You have no real influence on your fate, because the way other players allocate the action dice is based on their hand and you can't choose to play any other cards than one of the three you randomly draw from the deck. So you often end up doing something against your will because you have no other option. 

Overall- beautiful game, but it's really nothing more than luck. Which is a shame because it could have been a great game if only some rules were slightly changed.

RATING: 5
Don't play this game with only 2-3 players.  It really shines with 4-5.  I haven't tried it with 6.

This game is good if you have kids.  Otherwise, it's a family game, with light strategy (you do end up with interesting choices, but not too many or anything).  It's probably the best race-condition game.

What it really has going for it is theme.  It's really fun to look at, and move your little pirate ship around, and try to snag each other's booty (not while the children are looking, however!).  

It's funner if you're playing with light-hearted people who are going to play along with the pirate theme and make all sorts of remarks and not take things too seriously.  It wouldn't be very fun to play with a serious strategy game group.  Waaaay too random for that.

So it's a good game for what it is: a light, pirate-themed family game (so long as you play with at least 4 players).  But I do think Tom Vassel over-touted this one.

RATING: 6
The hand management of your actions both only being able to use each once or twice and also having to occasionally use an action that is actually bad for you causes some hard choices to have to be made in the game. At the same time the game is very accessible (albeit a bit too light for its game length) both in terms of easiness of rules and actually being good with 6 players.

I also like the need to manage your resources in able to move, as it feels realistic and also makes you sometimes have to choose with performing a mad dash or going slow and steady.

One negative I have of the game however is that it seems like gold isn't very useful early (and at times you might have to play a card that gives you gold early due to your limited card options), as often that just puts a huge target on your back for other people to plunder you.

RATING: 7
This game has a lot going for it, but it needs a little help. At it's core, Jamaica is just a beefed up, roll and move, racing game. There's a few decisions to make, but nothing to write home about. You need to add a little bit to make Jamaica work. Simply sitting down at the table, and staring at the board the whole game will make it seem quite dry and boring. You need to talk in pirate voices, goad other players into fighting you, cheer when you take the lead, etc. Nothing over the top, just add a little excitement to this game to make it come to life, and it works great!

RATING: 6.5
Received 08/21/08

Opened and punched. Artwork is, as expected, just simply awesome. Rules are a not very functional.  They fold out into a large poster so using them at the table to check rules is going to be a pain.

Okay...don't expect anything deep here but it's still fun.  You're always at the mercy of your cards and how the captain assigns the dice but hey...the game isn't rocket science.  You just bash your way to the end and hope for the best.  Obviously with more people you're going to be battling more.  

My one complaint is that the 'star' battle die is a killer and feels too powerful.

New complaint: The box is rather thin and has already split at two corners. And I'm even very careful with my games.

Traded Feb 13, 2014

RATING: 8
Jamaica is a fun pirate themed racing game.  In it players race their pirate ships around the island of Jamaica, while trying to feed their crew, gain treasures, and fight off other pirates!  The winner is not necessarily the one who gets around the island first, but the one who has gotten the most points.  Points are determined by your place at the end of the race, and how much gold and certain treasures you've found along the way.

This is arguably the most beautiful game ever produced.  The components and artwork are so very nice.  The game is fast and fun, and I really enjoy it.  It's the best race game I've ever played.  I highly recommend Jamaica to everyone.  Also, it makes for a great family game!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Simple, pleasant enough but, ultimately, uninvolving piece of fluff that would work well with youngish children. 

Roll two dice, decide which die represents the day action and which the night action. Play a card from your hand and take the actions shown (collect goods/treasures or move forward/back). Pay any costs from your holds if required by the space you land on. Battle other pirates if you land on their space.

If I had some kids, I might consider this as a family game because the artwork is nice and the piratical theme is quite fun with a 'take that' combat element and I guess that you'd enjoy it as a parent just to see the kids having a great time. 

The day/night action mechanism is nice and there are various ways to earn points as you race your ships around the island, but there are better race games for grown-ups.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Jamaica's a game with a lot of lighthearted fun and amazing artwork that's a delight to look at as the game goes on, but it falls into a weird category of games for me. It's very light - it's as light as you might want a filler micro game to be that takes maybe 15-20 minutes tops. There's almost no decision making, you're pretty much along for the ride in this game. It's a decently fun ride, but it being so light but taking an hour or sometimes more to play, by the end you're wishing it would end already. The combination of this game being so light but taking so long for such a light game means it has a hard time getting to the table over other games. If I want a light game I'm usually wanting a quick one, or quick ones are just more attractive. If I want a long game I want one with substance and decision making.

This game is great fun for one playthrough and no more. That one playthrough is a fantastic experience, between the elegant mechanics and the spectacular artwork, but while the mechanics are elegant they just aren't enough.

RATING: 7.7
This is an almost perfect light, family game - it is really well implemented.  A round starts by rolling 2 dice. The active player chooses the order with which all players use the dice.  Then all the players pick a card which best advances their position given the dice positions.  The movement is fun and interesting.  The combat is simple yet engaging.  The exploration aspects (with the treasure tiles) are also alluring and interesting.  Jamaica does everything really well!  It is light - really light even - but for what it is, it is first in it's class.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Jamaica, ehrm.. "Aargh ho ho ho and a bottle of... why is the rum gone!!?" Basically Jamaica is a racing game with pirate ships and cannons. You try to race around the island and fill your ship with gold. You also need food to feed your crew and cannonballs to fight your rivals. This isn`t merely a roll and move game but dice rolls determine how many commodities or gridmovements you can spend in the morning and in the evening. Every player can then program which antions they eill do by playing a card that illustrates the wanted actions.

Jamaica is a simple game but fun and theme works for me better than in for example Formula D.

RATING: 8
Video Review: https://youtu.be/bQzXSGL-Itk

Jamaica is mainly a racing game, but it plays out with a much more piratey gusto then one might expect. Using a clever system of dice and cards to determine how many of the two actions you get too do. On the way you will blast and steal from your opponents, while trying to maintain enough speed to get into that scoring zone. A fantastic and easy to learn game despite the unwieldy instructions.

OWN IT. Great great GREAT fun racing game. Everything I wanted in a pirate game and in a racing game. Now I have an accessible game that's fun and easy for everyone that's still interesting, has some strategies, an inlay for the box that actually works perfectly, cool art, great simple mechanics, and a good flow.

For what this game is trying to be, it achieves it perfectly. If you like pirate, racing, or casual games that are still board games and not party games, this 30-60 minute game is a complete winner!

RATING: 7
I haven't played many race games before so I don't have much to compare with. Overall I enjoyed playing Jamaica. There's an abundance of Caribbean themed games but I like it and I'm not tired of it yet. It was pretty stressful and tense to puzzle together the balance between gold, movement and whether to attack or avoid attacking.

A pretty short game, around an hour, but any more and I think it would have overstayed its welcome.

The rules were more complex than I thought even though it's a pretty light weight game. However, once you get playing it's fairly easy.

The rulebook is a disaster! Who thought that making the rulebook a map was a good idea? The rules are well written but the fold out map is horrible.

The old box artwork is way better than the new.

RATING: 5
A gorgeous game with simple rules that is easy to learn and quick to play.
 
I detest dice. Although this game is dependent on dice, all players share the same die rolls, (except in combat). Players use the few cards they have in their hands to make the best use of each roll to progress around the board, which takes some of the randomness out of the dice.

Has an excellent box insert that stores all components separately and securely. The instruction manual, while thematic, is as awkward as one of those fold-out road maps.

Unfortunately, the play really does feel like you are always trying to choose the least harmful of a small array of bad options. That, and the fact that, as in all racing games, there really is only a single path to victory, which limits replayability.

RATING: 7
It's a sort of racing game. Not a pure racing game as you can win without being in first position. Actually you could win by being in the last position in the "race".

Mechanically the game is a hidden action selection with dices deciding how valuable actions are (dices are thrown first so you know them). In movement you need to balance between gold and food to be able to get ahead. You'd also like to have some cannons to be able to enchance your odds in battles (one throw of a die for both parties). There is a high luck factor especially in battles and especially with 6 players. You cannot know for sure how other will move and you might be forced to have battles you don't want.

The game is chaotic with 6 players but it definitely needs at least 4 to be fun and I'd prefer to play with 5 or 6 when given chance. Not for too serious gaming but a fun racing game.

RATING: 7
Rated after one play.

The components and packaging are fantastic... this is an exemplar of great component design, especially the molded insert... never seen one better. (Important Exception is the rules, which thematically unfolds like a big treasure map but is pretty annoying to read in the first place or to use as a reference during a game.) The art is absolutely gorgeous... I am floored by the paintings.

The game (played with 3 others) was okay, but players didn't seem to feel like they were really "doing" anything. The player who won didn't feel like she had done anything particularly clever to earn the win, and the rest of us felt similarly about our unsuccessful performances.

It's a decent game with bonus points for sheer beauty. I would like to try it again, perhaps with younger (read: 8-12 year-olds.) I think it could function well with players of that age, or mixed between that age and older.

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (4):[/COLOR]

[i]Wow, what a bummer this game was, I really don't get the hype that surrounded this game. Note to self... don't believe the hype surrounding OOP games! RATING: 7

I like the fact that of the characters one can chose to play, all are actual historical figures.  Two of these are even female!  Although this is basically just a race around the board, there are lots of elements that keep it from being dull.  For one thing, the separate day and night phases of each turn, the risk of finding cursed treasure as you seek to augment your score, the challenge of keeping yourself supplied with the essentials (food, gold and gunpowder) with only limited space in your hold, and the menacing presence of the ghost ship (in the two-player game, the only one I've played).  My maiden voyage was a little long, but that was largely my own fault.  I'm sure with people who have played the game before, things move along at a snappier pace. (4+3)

RATING: 8.1
This is one gorgeously produced awesome game! This is one great pirate race! The unique card mechanic is simple and fun. The treasures are fun with both good and cursed treasures. Wonderful battle mechanic too! The first player rolls 2 D6, the results become the day and night conditions. Each player plays a card with the intention to move forward or backward, get food, get cannons, or gold. What ever card is played determines your turn events. Sometimes you move, sometimes you collect things. Whenever a player lands on a space with another player a battle must take place, allowing the winner to steal from the other ships holds...or give the loser your cursed treasure...Arrrgh! Certain board spaces require payment in food or gold. So planning is wise in holding your cards. The person with the most points in gold wins!

RATING: 7
心得:
非常簡單的遊戲
樂趣可能要在人多互動打來打去才有
不然就是想辦法收集資源往前衝而已
規則:
*寶藏卡洗云12取9放圖板中央，九個寶藏標記放圖板海盜穴，骰子放對應位置
*每個人拿一艘船方起始點(逆時鐘賽跑)，對應腳色卡洗勻蓋著抽三張跟一個船艙上面選兩格放3食物跟3元，隨機起始
*遊戲由多輪組成，當有玩家跑完一圈結束，每輪四個階段
1.船長(起始玩家)擲骰，並決定怎麼放
2.每個人秘密選擇一張卡出
3.牌打開 根據順位執行上面的動作(先執行右邊在執行左邊，個數看左右的骰子)
>裝載物品時要放到空的格子，如果都滿就要先棄掉，不能棄掉跟要裝得一樣的物品
>前後移動對應格數後要支付該格的費用，如果遇到人先戰鬥再支付(白格一格一個食物)
*戰鬥由移動方先決定要出幾個火藥在擲骰，再由防禦方做一樣的事情，平手沒事，數字大的從小的懲罰3擇1，拿他一格物品/偷他寶藏卡/給他寶藏卡，星號視為直接勝利(戰鬥方擲到的話防禦方就不用擲了)
*資源不夠付的話先全付，然後退到某格你能付得停在那(可退到海盜穴)
*海盜穴免費且有寶藏標記的可棄掉拿一張寶藏卡，有效果的翻開沒效果的蓋著放
4.回合結束該牌棄掉抽一張新的，起始換人
*遊戲在有人過終點該回合結束後結束，加總所在位置的分數跟所有黃金還有寶藏分，分數高的獲勝(-5之後的都算-5)，平手比誰跑得遠
*牌不夠抽就洗勻重建牌庫
*裝載時如果全滿又跟要裝得一樣就不能裝
*起始格不會有戰鬥
*多人同格由停的人決定要跟誰打
*重擲寶藏卡第二擲不能加火藥，可逼人家重擲
****2人****
*使用黑船當NPC，並獲得+2火藥寶藏卡(不能被偷)，船上在一格5元1格3元，第3階段所有人結束後根據骰子移動他兩次，最後就前進，最前面就後退，中間就由船長決定，叉口也是船長決定，停在海盜穴有寶藏就拿，戰鬥結束後懲罰由對面玩家決定，只有拿黃金會放在船上

RATING: 6
While it's perhaps a touch too far to say that this game plays itself, your choices are constricted and your fate is in the lap of the dice gods. Your cards have a left side and a right side with a symbol in each - food, gold, cannons, movement. Play one of your 3 cards secretly, the start player rolls 2 dice and allocates 1 left, 1 right, and whatever he placed, that's what you get from your card when you reveal. So if you play a move/move and a 6/5 gets rolled, happy days and you're well on the way to completing the lap of the board that's required (VPs are earnt depending how far you get around when the first player gets home). If he rolls a 1/1, you're in deep stoop because you only have so many move cards and your best one's wasted. That's the game. Most spaces require payment in gold or food, otherwise you move backwards until you hit a pay-free spot, so you need to consistently load up. Cannons you'll use whenever you land on someone or someone lands on you - each one can add 1 to your die in the dice-off that follows, winner gets to steal stuff from the other. So the game is 2 steps forward, 1 step back all the way, and occasionally 1 step forward, 2 steps backwards. It's fluffy and goes decently fast and if you like dice-based races, this is a nice twist on the genre. Just don't emotionally invest though.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.2

RATING: 2.5
A racing game, where you're traveling around an island, feeding your crew, collecting treasures, attacking other ships and lotting gold. In the game, you're selecting through 3 action cards, which have two actions (one for the morning and one for the evening), and to decide how much you're going to do from your action, you're throwing dice.

It's a game quite dominated by luck, as battles are also decided by a single die (adjusted by the number of the cannons you have). It's light, ok to play, but too much luck for me and not enough fun.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

This is a simple, yet fun pirate game.  Sadly, it's probably one of the best pirate games out there.  It's highly interactive, many different paths to win, little downtime, and a lot of fun against your opponents.

The game can have big swings and some of the treasures are over powered and transfer players.  If looking for a "more serious" pirate game, this might not satisfy you.

RATING: 7
When I bought it I thought it was something [i]completely different[/i]. It doesn't matter really 'cause this [i]is[/i] a fun game. I know I say this about quite many games, but [b]Jamaica[/b] is really beautiful, almost [i]stunning[/i]. That's already reason [i]enough[/i] to play it. The game itself is a very easy and laid back [b]familygame[/b] about pirates racing around an island, collecting treasures and looting eachother. There's one problem with this game as I see it; it's a tad [i]too[/i] long for what it's worth and that also affects how often you want to play it. If you want a game to play once or twice every half year or so; [i]this is it[/i]!

RATING: 6
Not too bad a game.  Has some fairly balanced mechanics, and is actually pretty fun.  Though, of course, the solid mechanics (use of holds, everyone has own deck, payment for food vs. gold) are knocked for a big loop by a lot of luck (the "auto-win" battle die, treasure draws, and, to a lesser extent, cards in hand when game nears end) and chaos (day vs. night die choices).  It's also got a lot of fiddly rules, which I suspect makes it difficult to "get" for newbies.  Still, it's fun and doesn't take very long.

RATING: 8
Beautiful game, wonderfully thematic. One of my favorites for small groups. It is a racing type game with a unique but familiar roll and move mechanic. The Night and Day portion is awesome, and allows from some really interesting plays. The game is quick paced as everyone plays every turn, and it works great with 4+. Did I mention the theme? =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A one lap race around the titular island in which you have to pay food/gold where you stop otherwise go back to where you can cough up. First past line ends game, with pts for placing plus coins in your storage equals vp score. Although it has Pirates Cove production values, this game provides a similar pirate experience in a shorter playing time, and is more of a resource management game as you only have limited storage and must discard excess (unless you pick up a spare space from landing on a treasure token). There are fights involving powder and a die roll, allowing the victor to pillage a storage space/treasure. Interesting action pt system via dice roll and card played. May well fit the niche for a pirate game for 4 to 6 as Caribbean satifies my pirate needs for 2 to 3 players.

RATING: 6
Cute racing game where you sail boats around an island through the playing of action cards. There are multiple routes, and the longer routes have better rewards in points than the shorter routes. It gets more challenging that each space has a cost associated with stopping there, so you need to manage your resources.

One issue is whenever you land on an opponent's space, you MUST fight them, which can get annoying if you land on someone who is much more combat prepared than you are. Overall a fun time-waster though. Not too thinky (sadly).

:star: Art and components
:star: Innovative mechanics
:star: Handles 5 or more players
:star: Good with different player counts
:star: Low time between turns
:nostar: Comfortable complexity
:nostar: Re-playability
:star::nostar::nostar: Enjoyment

RATING: 7.5
A fun light racing game that can't quite decide whether it wants to be luck based or skill based. The art is beautiful and the components are very well done. There are interesting decisions to make and plans to lay, but there are also elements that are very swingy like combat being resolved by a single unmitigated die roll. I don't mind luck-based games, but when there are a lot of thoughtful decisions in the rest of the game, the swingy luck elements annoy me. Still, it's a fun game overall and if you don't worry about winning and losing it works well.

Première impression:
Jamaica est une jeu léger, très plaisant pour toute la famille. Le matériel est superbe. Les règles sont bien expliquées, simples et faciles à lire un quelques minutes. Il y a beaucoup de chance impliquée ce qui peut déplaire aux joueurs expérimentés. Il y a tout de même une part de gestion dans ce jeu de sorte que ce n'est pas juste une partie de chance. Les batailles sont drôles et pas trop endicapentes pour le perdant. J'ai bien hâte d'y rejouer.
Après quelques parties, c'est vraiement un bon jeu famillial je ne changerai pas mon évaluation.

RATING: 7.8
I am really not sure about this one. Initially I thought this was a stunningly well produced pirate themed racing game. It has some outstanding properties and visuals. The box and the board are fantastically imaginative. Just what you would dream of in a perfect pirate game.The box insert is cleverly though out and the space is used exceptionally well. The components are very high quality.Everything is visually perfect. Nothing stands out of place with this game except for the movement mechanism. I do like it, but we have played this game maybe 4-5 times and I am just perplexed with the movement.I find that the movement is slow around the board,it's funny how it feels like a sailing ship. Slow and steady around the board. Collecting coins and treasures as you progress. But I can't seem to influence the speed at which the ship moves. Its purely down to the luck of the cards and how they are played. I would love to play this more but it leaves me feeling a little frustrated that I wasn't able to do anything to encourage the win. Maybe I don't understand the cards too .It would be nice if you had the ability to go after / seek out your opponents. With a bit more intent. The dice do a good job but something is just not right.

This is a great game to play with my family (2 young boys and my wife).  The components look excellent, the theme (Pirates!) goes over very well with my sons, and it plays relatively quickly.  Is it lightweight? Yep.  Does luck play a factor? Absolutely.  Is it fun? Yes, it is.  If you are looking for a brain-burning strategy game then keep on looking, but if you are looking for a fun game to play with young gamers,non-gamers, or gamers wanting a lighter title - give this one a play.  Plus, you can talk like a pirate when you play it :D.

Update: ticked down a notch to 7.  Still really enjoy it as a family game, though.

RATING: 3
Totally hated it. Your turn will be 95% dictated by other players. When you gets a say during the other 5% it may or may not work out anyway 

leader rolls 2 dice, decides which dice corresponds to day/night and everyone plays event card. For example, leader rolled 4 & 6, decides 4 = day and 6 = night, you play 1 card (say day = move, night = gold). Then you'll move 4 during day and gain 6 gold during night. Problem? What if you need to move 3 or 5 to avoid getting beaten up by other people (move to same location = auto-combat)? 

Beautiful art, terrible game

RATING: 2
A racing game where actions are extremely swing-y.  Movement doesn't always go the way you plan, and combat can be won by rolling a specific side of the die no matter how set for combat your opponent is (which is nice when it works in your favor, but I dislike games that imply you can gear up for an action only to have your opponent completely negate it with a lucky roll).  This leads to frustration as nothing seems to go the way you plan, which is nice for catch-up mechanics.  However, making the race close at the expense of player agency isn't a solution I like.
