RATING: N/A
I'll reserve a rating until I've had more playthroughs. I have played this once so far using the two player rules with my wife.

The theming and art for Jamaica is absolutely top notch. If you're looking for a game that oozes character and charm, this is it. Fantastic artwork, and high quality pieces and printing make this game shine.

After a first playthrough it's pretty clear that this game works best the more interaction between players there is. The more combat, the tighter the race, the more interesting and tense the experience. Unfortunately I felt the need to intentionally play sub-optimally to keep the first playthrough fun for both my wife and I. I attacked the Ghost Ship (a limited control AI player necessary for 2 player games) when it served no purpose, I chose to play cards that moved me forward more slowly because it was way too easy to get too far ahead with the right die rolls and card draw. My wife was sick the first time we played and I wanted her to enjoy the experience without feeling like I totally crushed her. I still had fun, but it was annoying to feel I had to hamper my own efforts to keep it fun for her.

Technically this game can be played with two people, but it's clearly better the more players you have. A wonderfully themed game that's fairly quick to play and easy to learn, but it has its issues.

RATING: 7.3
Jamaica -- Played twice; three- and four-player.

Neat mechanism.  Cards have different left and right indexes.  Active player rolls two dice and determines which die applies to which index, then the rest of the players choose which card to use, with the dice results applying to their cards left to right.

Very nice production values and component quality.  In fact, Jon particularly liked that the cover of the instruction booklet depicts only coins, so that when you open the box (which looks like a treasure chest), all you see are doubloons.  Thoughtful implementation.

RATING: 1
This game has a good buzz, so I was somewhat overwhelmed when I finally tried it. 

Firstly it's TTR category game (weight, target audience), but it's less accessible. Jamaica is a race game around the island, where you get some money for where you finish and every money and treasure grabbed along the way also counts. However the cards (two actions, one for morning one for evening) aren't the most intuitive.

And it drags. I have no idea what with the race games, but most of them are so slow. This one requires some residence management, some counting the board, some figuring our which card to take and all takes time. And all of these confuse kids with whom I'd play a game like this. 

There is combat where you can steal each other's treasure (or give them your cursed treasure) and that part is okay. It's just kinda random to arrange it. 

Too much overhead for what should be a light romp and it drags as a consequence. 

EDIT: eh. Down to 1.0. Just don't see validation for this game to exist. Too complicated and too slow for it wants to be, hence: half finished.

RATING: 7
This is a racing game where players each play a pirate using the rolls of dice to collect resources and advance around an island.  It is really easy to teach, has some nice mechanics, and plays in about 30 minutes making it a fantastic filler.

Each player controls a pirate ship with 5 holds and a deck of cards, of which players have 3 in their hand at a time.  At the beginning of a round a player rolls two dice and assigns them to a "morning" and "evening" action.  Each card depicts two actions, one occurring during the morning and one during the evening phase.  These actions are either moving forward, backward, or collecting one of the 3 resources in the game.  The dice dictate how many spaces you move or resources you collect.  Most of the spaces cost gold or food to land on or you're pushed back and the third resource is gunpowder which is used in combat if you land on an opponent's ship during an action.

That's pretty much it.  The game ends when a player makes a full circuit of the map and players are awarded points based on their final position, number of gold, and certain treasures.  Some of the spaces around the board also contain treasures, it usually requires moving more spaces to collect the treasures but they can give end-game points or bonuses during the game.  Some are cursed as well, however, subtracting points at the end of the game.

This is clearly a roll-and-move game which by default garnishes boos from most gamers but this is a proper design with that mechanic.  Sure, you are moving due to the whim of a dice roll but there is a modicum of control and choice associated with that movement.  You have 3 cards to choose from and two ways to order the dice when it is your turn to roll.  There are still going to be rounds where all your options are sub-par but for this type of game that's okay.

I think this is a wonderful filler game.  That's all it is but it plays super quick, is easy to teach, and it looks really nice as well.  The components are all colorful and pretty and the insert holds everything is fitted spaces which is excellent.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is a race game on the surface, but there is a whole lot bubbling underneath that makes it a fun, dynamic, competitive strategy game. You need to manage several different aspects at once: resource management of food, gunpowder, and doubloons in your limited hull; movement to the optimal board spaces for your current situation; stockpiling enough resources to get by but not so many that you waste them; using up precious gunpowder attacking or defending; and much more. Race as your favorite plundering pirate to discover invaluable treasures, steal from your competitors, feed your crew, pay for port services, attack other ships, and curse your competition! 

Each round consists of that round's captain rolling two dice and selecting which to play for the morning action and which to play for the evening action. Then each player, starting with the captain, chooses which of their action cards to play to either move or collect a resource (food, doubloons, or gunpowder) based on the face-up number on each die. This is a very fun aspect of the game and necessitates some moderate planning ahead to see if any of your action cards have a movement to get you a treasure card or a particular resource that is running low in your hull.  

As you travel around the map, you must pay food to travel on the sea and doubloons to land at a port. You have to be careful, though, because if you move to a spot where you can't afford to pay, you must pay all you can of that resource then move back until you land on a space where you can pay everything...and then you have to pay that, too. See if you can use this to your advantage to land on treasure spaces at a very cheap cost!  

Another fun feature that I love about Jamaica is how a battle is forced every time two players land in the same spot. A star rolled on either side is an automatic win. Do you use six gunpowder tokens to really ramp up your attack so you can steal that player's treasure card or food tokens just to get blown away by a single star roll? Or should you play conservatively relying on the luck of the die? 

Overall, this is a very fun, pirate-themed game with incredible artwork and very high-quality pieces and boards. I give it a solid 8.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
I've tried to like this game both times I've played it. It's cute, colourful, and the components are top-notch for a great price! Also, this is the first game box I've ever seen where every component has its own place- no spillover or loose cards falling around. If I were rating it on components it would get a 10.

But the game is ridiculously luck-based, and apparently I get the worst hands imaginable, combined with truly teeth-clenching dice rolls. The second time I played it, my first 3 turns I had no movement cards, and then when I finally got movement cards (the forward/back cards, not the elusive forward/forward card) the dice continuously showed up as N and N+1, meaning that I could move a maximum of 1 space backwards or forwards in my current state.

Needless to say, I was saying "Yargh!" the whole game- and not in the fun Pirate-y way.

RATING: 8
The visuals: this is what immediately jumps out at you about this game!  Every little bit of the game, from the box itself to the cards which can be placed end-to-end to form one long picture, has had a great deal of effort put into every minute detail.  I just love those visuals - this is cartoonish artwork done right (are you listening, "BattleLore"?)!  The only annoying thing about all that is the inconvenient "treasure map" style rules booklet.  And the icing on the cake is the fact that they have even put a great deal of thought into creating the best box insert that I have ever seen!  But enough gushing over the physical components - it's all well and good to have a pretty game, but is the game itself good?  And the answer is YES, as long as you don't mind something light, quick, and fun, that has fairly minimal strategic choices.  In fact, "Jamaica" is pretty much at the top of my list of gateway games now because it is very easy to learn, can be played in an hour, and is a fun, albeit light, experience even for a more experienced gamer such as myself.  The only thing that doesn't make much sense to me about game play is the fact that every player is supposed to do both their morning and evening actions before the next player plays.  We now play that all players take their morning action, then everyone takes their evening action.  And to get the most out of this game, you probably want to have at least 4-5 players.  But in a nutshell, this is a gorgeous, fun, light game.  Game design: 5/5  Personal enjoyment: 3/5  Total: 8/10

RATING: 6
[GameWorks SàRL 07 edition (1st printing) w/ Essen 08 promo cards] {Pirate, gateway; dice-rolling, resource management, fighting; optimal 4-6p} Jamaica is a wondrous family game.  It is thematic, fun and interactive.  It is not a strategic game and in most cases, your decisions are bound by the cards in hand and dice rolls.  In addition, the mechanic to resolve a battle is highly luck, though simple, due to the "explosion" (star).  It is a good gateway game - fun, fast, language-independent, dynamic, etc.  However, the game is a little bit too long with 5-6 players. 2p game is just boring. It is better to play this game with 4 players.  Besides, luck is very strong in this game (treasure card draw, dice rolls, etc.) and gamers may not really like this game.

Nonetheless, it is a tactical resource management game.  Players need to smartly maintain gold and food for their ships.  The racing aspect is also important - leading the race is a viable strategy.

The game is excellently produced: attractive, colorful and cute illustration, big dice, charming pirate ships, etc.  I particular like the cards can be assembled to form a story.

RATING: 9.5
Beatiful simple game with great artwork, just what i want in a boardgame, light fun and appealing. A big hit in my game group, the only downside that its combat is too dice roll dependant... I sometimes do a houserule to minimize the luck dependant with normal 1-6 dice with 6 is critical hit... this way the gunpowder will be more useful in combat and reduce random luck dice rolling to minimum.
Also a little rant about the rulebook... mine comes with multi language copies rule book, and I dont see it necessary... its just adds weight to the game, and I ended up spending a lot of money for the shipping cost to my country, If only those other 3 or 4 non english rule book doesnt included, it will be around 2KG weight and perfect for normal price shipping.
Despite that, this is my number one game for fun light game, thanks Jamaica for the fun hours spent with you.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The art design in this game is BAR NONE the most stunning thing I have ever seen in a board game!!!  The action cards create a panorama longer than the table you are likely playing on.  The gold coins on the back of the rulebook make the box feel like opening a treasure chest.  All of the components fit perfectly into their own slots, with the treasure cards being 'hidden' under the player mats like...buried treasure.  The rulebook itself opens up into a treasure map.  The board is gorgeous and intricately decorated.  I have never seen this kind of cohesion in art design...in anything I've ever seen before.  

The game itself is a swashbuckling race against your fellow pirates around the island of Jamaica.  Gameplay is simple, but compelling due to the racing component and the battling you will do with your salty pirate rivals. 

Any lack of depth in the gameplay is made up for in the art direction and jokes made at the table with your fellow pirates.  Everyone should play this game at least once in my opinion.  It is a phenomenal experience.

RATING: 6.5
Played once with 5 players and once with 3 players. 5 or 6 is probably the sweet spot. originally designed to be given to Swiss insurance company clients. Since the game was really well received, the insurance company decided to release it to the general public (only in Europe currently). The game has some amazingly beautiful components and the board showing one main island and some smaller ones along the edge is very nicely done. The game play is pretty simple. A player rolls two dice and places one of them on the Day slot and the other on the Night slot. Then each player chooses a card from his hand of 3 cards to play. Each card has an action associated with Day and one with Night. The cards are then resolved in player order. A player may end up moving forward and/or backward some number of spaces, collect food, gun powder or doubloons. When a player moves, the space where he lands is resolved. If there is a food or doubloon payment there, a player must pay it or move backwards until he lands on a space that he can pay. If there is a treasure there, he draws a treasure card which will provide either doubloons, curses or special powers. If a player lands on a space occupied by another player, a battle ensues. In a battle, players may spend gunpowder to add to their attack roll. Whoever wins the battle steals the contents from one of the defeated pirate's 5 hold spaces. The game ends at the end of the round when one player makes it around the board. Doubloons and treasures are added to the bonus number on the space at which a pirate ends.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
One of the best pirate games out there, though it's strictly a racing affair. It's gorgeous and fun artwork suck you in, the mechanics are fast and easy to understand, and the games play quickly with virtually no downtime. Bonus points go to the amazing interior box design. If you're a pirate fan, pick this one up.

RATING: 8
First of all, fantastic production.  Beautiful from the components to to the insert.

This is just the kind of game that I can easily get to the table as it is fun for both kids and adults, easy to teach, looks great, has a theme with broad appeal, scales well from 3-6 players and plays within an hour. 

Basically it is the perfect family game.

Update: Rating goes from a 7.5 to an 8. I find every play to be fun and the game plays out differently all of the time. Some games people are more bunched up due to cards, dice rolls, strategy, whatever. Those games have a lot of combat and fortunes are swinging wildly. Other games are spread out and the racing takes precedence. And some times there are some racers and some fighters. 

However it plays out, it is rarely clear who the winner will be. As I said, great fun!

This one has moved right up there with Around the World in 80 Days for favorite family boardgame.




Suitability for Travel:

I have a 1 to 5 scale for four categories (1 is worst, 5 is best) in order of importance:

Portability (the less luggage space the better) - 1
Footprint (the less table space when playing the better) - 1
Scalability (the wider range of player counts the better) - 4
Learnability (the easier to teach non-gamers the better) - 3


Overall - 1

RATING: 6
I would characterize Jamaica as a very light race-around-the-board pirate dice game. Because there are a finite number of spots on the track, this game plays quickly and well under an hour even with five. There are some shades of similarity between this game and Pirate's Cove apart from the theme. I personally like this game better than Pirate's Cove which has a significant rich-get-richer problem and that the first player to lose several battles have a tough time coming back to win. The dice mechanic is cute but not sure if it contributes that much to the game in terms of mechanic. The sea battles are streamlined and even though I appreciate the rapid battles, they are very luck-driven. Early gains in cargo holds don't mean much but later cargo holds have to be mainly doubloons. Overall an ok game which deserves occasional play.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.7
You try to be the first to reach the finish line but at the same time you try to collect points and treasures while racing for the win.
Everyone has three cards in his hands and every card shows two values (move, fight etc.). You have to use both values on the card you play.
There is an interesting mechanism where the starting player rolls dice and can decide which die to put on the day phase (first value to use) and night phase (second value).
According to these values, the players plan their turn and which card to choose and which action to use when.
Despite this interesting mechanism (I've never seen it in any other game so far) it was just not my game, I think it could be very cool but somehow I didn't enjoy it very much.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Probably too light and fluffy for regular appearances at your game group, but a great game for the family.  There's many games that have tried for the pirate theme, and this is the first light game that has succeeded.  If you're a pirate fan, you can get by with this game for the lighter evenings, and [gameid=25292] for the heavy side.  

Jamaica's mechanics are dead simple, and decisions are straightforward without being strategically obvious.  There's a bit of take-that gameplay, but it's light enough and not crushing enough so that it can be recovered from rather easily.  

Finally, the artwork on the cards is absolutely gorgeous, as every card in a player's deck is uniquely illustrated in a luscious style.  They are perfectly executed, and it's pleasant getting lost in the art whenever you find yourself with some downtime.  It's the best execution of lighthearted cartoon art in a boardgame that I know of.  Really a triumph.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

I like the way the cards, the dice, and the day/night rules coincide, but the randomness of the cards mixed with the randomness of the dice can create some frustrating moments, especially when you have no cargo in your hulls.  Still, the production of the game gives it a lot of OOMPH, and the game is short enough that it doesn't overstay its welcome.  If you're looking for a real pirate-y game, though, you might want to look elsewhere, since the theme is pretty much just for show.

2 plays: 5 players

In 1675, after a long career in piracy, Henry Morgan skillfully gets appointed Governor of Jamaica, with the explicit order to cleanse the Caribbean of pirates and buccaneers !
\13\\13\
Instead, he invites all of his former "colleagues" and comrades-in-arms to join him in his retirement, so they can enjoy the fruits of their looting in all impunity.
\13\\13\
Each year, in remembrance of the "good old days", Morgan organizes the Great Challenge, a race around the island, and at its end the Captain with the most gold in his holds is declared Grand Winner.

RATING: 6
This is a family friendly roll and move game. In other words, kryptonite to most hobby gamers. It seems like it is going to be underwhelming as expected all of the way through the rules explanation, but then you start playing, and happily the game delivers a much more interesting experience. Most of this is due to the contrived rules about storing and using cargo on your ship, as the game forces you to work out clever moves to minimize the loss of resources. The action selection/hand management mechanics also combo nicely with the cargo rules to give you a bit more to think about from turn to turn than you might expect.

All that being said, it is still very much a simple to teach family game. Even the newest recruit will be able to pick up the rules after one run around the table. It's also effectively a race game, which makes it super easy for a new player to understand 'how to win', which is often times the hardest thing to communicate when explaining a new game.

If you're looking for a great gateway game, give this one a try!

RATING: 6
This is a great little roll-and-move race game with a few twists: you're rolling dice for the whole table, then using cards that have two symbols and lining those up with the dice, so the order of the dice matters. There's also a bit of combat if you ever land on the same space as another player. Beyond that, it's a simple game of trying to get back to the starting line as soon as possible and being able to pay the tolls along the way.

It's a beautiful game with fantastic art and a friendly pirate theme, one that I'll keep around for a quick game or for new gamers.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
HARRRR!!!! piraterij was nog nooit zo simpel.

Spelers zijn piraten die rond het eiland jamaica varen in een wedstrijd. Echter als ze elkaar tegenkomen zullen ze er alles aan doen om de tegestanders uit te schakelen in een vuurgevecht. Daarnaast zijn er ook nog verschillende schatten te vinden rond het eiland, maar kijk uit dat ze niet vervloekt zijn.

Iedere ronde rolt één speler twee dobbelstenen en aan de hand van die dobbelstenen speelt iedere speler een actiekaart uit met twee acties erop. Deze acties kunnen zijn: verplaatsen, kanonskogels aanschaffen, voedsel en geld inslaan. Aan het eind wint de speler met de meeste punten, die kan men krijgen door geld, schatten en de eindpositie in de race.

Pretty pirate-themed racing game that offers some opportunities for clever play and tangling with other players, but the randomness of the movement card selection prevents this from being anything more than a light, breezy game. Claiming victory comes down more to having the right cards at the right time rather than superior tactics. But losses from having the wrong cards at the wrong times, aren't so painful.

RATING: 6
A very well designed and smart game for the family to be sure.  The simple roll-and-move concept was further improved upon by the clever designation between a day and night choice for all players.  The decision was then expanded by the cards in your hand.  There was a smidgen of the RoboRally-esque sense of chaos in that what happened each round (in terms of where you move to) may not always be what you have planned.  The backward penalty for not having enough resources to pay was interesting but also easily abused.  Sure there was a huge amount of luck involved, but some of it was controllable.

Like I said, Jamaica is a fine game for the right audiences but alas I'm not really one of them.  So while I don't mind playing it occasionally, it is definitely not a must have title for me.

RATING: 7.5
WOW! What a fantastic components are in this game. The ships, the artwork on the cards (notice that when you place them one behind another in the right order, there is a big painting), the components (which fit perfectly into the boxinsert), the rules which looks like a treasure map (which made them not easier to read, but it’s great addition to the theme of the game). Everything just looks like this is a game for adults to play with kids. After playing this one, we only can agree. Easy to explain. Fun to play. Fantastic theme. What could a parent want more to introduce their kids into boardgaming? Or if you have no kids, just use it to introduce it to other non-boardgamers.

RATING: 6.5
I would say that this game is ranked closer to what I define to be a 7.

I think the components are top-notch and very attractive, durable, and thematic.  I couldn't be happier with the production quality of this game!

The gameplay is somewhat lacking.  Don't get me wrong, I find the game to be fun, but not as exciting as many reviews stated.  

If you are looking for a lighter game with a pirate theme, this is an excellent choice.  BUT if you are looking for a more tactacle experience, this falls flat.

Families will love this one though and I can see it being a staple in many board game collections.

RATING: 8.5
A game done right! Great theme, great artwork, simple rules, only symbols - no reading required (on the cards or anywhere else), interesting choices to make on every turn, right amount of luck for the gamelength (just go for a "Revanche" if your cannons fly low - or go for a best out of 3 from the start). Interesting risk-reward mechanism (especially for the later players, since it can happen that the required resource for your plan is taken from you).

Don´t play with whiners or hotheads - other than that: simply great fun!

Only reasons to not award 10 Points: I can sometimes be frustrating/anticlimactic if the leading player(s) make it way beond the other players. Rules as a folding-map might be a thematic idea - but is simply a pain.
